  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253535496?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Antoinette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Antoinette" href="/user/show/5328952-antoinette">Antoinette</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3246743145?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/5512657-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=2020-aty-challenge">2020-aty-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=detective">detective</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3246743145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8406837020975946755">I am not a fan of detective novels or police procedurals, but this was written by Kate Atkinson and I have found her other books marvelously inventive and never boring. I’m glad I decided to chance it, because Jackson Brodie is an individual, not a cliche, and Atkinson’s approach to this genre is different than most, as well.<br/><br/>Jackson is a private detective with four cases, and they are different cases, just as a real detective might have. Each of them is interesting and each solved in a realistic</span>
  <span id="freeText8406837020975946755" style="display:none">I am not a fan of detective novels or police procedurals, but this was written by Kate Atkinson and I have found her other books marvelously inventive and never boring. I’m glad I decided to chance it, because Jackson Brodie is an individual, not a cliche, and Atkinson’s approach to this genre is different than most, as well.<br /><br />Jackson is a private detective with four cases, and they are different cases, just as a real detective might have. Each of them is interesting and each solved in a realistic way. I loved the way Atkinson weaved between the cases, revealing clues to us as they were revealed to Brodie, and allowing us an opportunity to put together the pieces. I confess, with delight, that I did not solve a single one of them ahead of the reveal. <br /><br />I seldom want to go on to a second book in a series like this. I loved the Jesse Stone movies, but I left Robert Parker’s books after only one attempt to become interested; I heard nothing but good things about Tana French, but Cassie Maddox left me flat. I’m thinking I haven’t had enough of Jackson Brodie, he’s interesting enough to make me want to see what becomes of him. Who would have guessed?<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8406837020975946755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1450508686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15721149461450988050">Gahhh, what a mess. The three "case histories" are "connected" by complete coincidence, and only the tiniest possible amount, the characters are complete caricatures and the entire plot was contrived and overblown. I've heard a lot about Kate Atkinson, most of it amazing, but this does not tempt me to read any more of her books... Though it could be worse, I suppose. At least she can string a coherent sentence together.<br/><br/>NOTE: I have since read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15790842.Life_After_Life' title='Life After Life by Kate Atkinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Life After Life</a> and it is <i>worlds</i> away from this mess.</span>
  <span id="freeText15721149461450988050" style="display:none">Gahhh, what a mess. The three "case histories" are "connected" by complete coincidence, and only the tiniest possible amount, the characters are complete caricatures and the entire plot was contrived and overblown. I've heard a lot about Kate Atkinson, most of it amazing, but this does not tempt me to read any more of her books... Though it could be worse, I suppose. At least she can string a coherent sentence together.<br /><br />NOTE: I have since read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15790842.Life_After_Life" title="Life After Life by Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Life After Life</a> and it is <i>worlds</i> away from this mess. Her writing there is wry and delicate, the story strung together with warmth and ease and I actually can't believe the same author wrote this book. Still, I'm glad I didn't give up on her completely - I suppose <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3722183.A_God_in_Ruins" title="A God in Ruins by Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener">A God in Ruins</a> is next!</span>

<div id="review_100373933" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100373933" />
    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3642045-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1274829293p2/3642045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100373933?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/3642045-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">mystery lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=britain">britain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100373933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5937663518317886544">This is the second of Atkinson's Jackson Brodie mystery novels I've read. I've previously enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/501124.One_Good_Turn' title='One Good Turn by Kate Atkinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>One Good Turn</a>. To briefly summarize what others have already mentioned, in this novel, Brodie takes on three cold cases and deals with a variety of individuals who vary from eccentric to criminal, from engaging to seemingly insane. Their stories, and the stories of the old crimes, are set up carefully and with wonderful detail, wending their ways back and forth through the book. We see the story thr</span>
  <span id="freeText5937663518317886544" style="display:none">This is the second of Atkinson's Jackson Brodie mystery novels I've read. I've previously enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/501124.One_Good_Turn" title="One Good Turn by Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener">One Good Turn</a>. To briefly summarize what others have already mentioned, in this novel, Brodie takes on three cold cases and deals with a variety of individuals who vary from eccentric to criminal, from engaging to seemingly insane. Their stories, and the stories of the old crimes, are set up carefully and with wonderful detail, wending their ways back and forth through the book. We see the story through multiple viewpoints, with Jackson being the center point and ultimately a sort of slightly flawed moral compass.<br /><br />I am amazed at what Atkinson has accomplished with this book, keeping all these stories alive and bouncing in the air with multiple narrators along side the central narrator. And doing this, she keeps the reader not only engaged but anxious to know what is going to happen next and to whom. And why? And what happened 34 years ago? or 10? And the other thing I found....I really cared what happened to all of them, including to Jackson.<br /><br />Oh---and I will continue reading this series.<br /><br />Probably a 4.5. Part of me wonders if it's a 5.<br /><br />Recommended for anyone who would like to read a literate mystery.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5937663518317886544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2896941723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15544149196266136591"><strong>Overrated</strong><br/><br/>This is the first book by Kate Atkinson that I have read. I was torn between giving it 3 or 4 stars, but I ended up going with 3 stars, because the book didn't live up to my expectations.<br/>Case Histories concerned 3 cold cases that Jackson Brodie has been hired to solve. Jackson Brodie used to be a police inspector but now works as a private investigator. The 3 cases all intersect at some point. One case is especially shocking.<br/>I watched the TV series based on this book but it only lasted </span>
  <span id="freeText15544149196266136591" style="display:none"><strong>Overrated</strong><br /><br />This is the first book by Kate Atkinson that I have read. I was torn between giving it 3 or 4 stars, but I ended up going with 3 stars, because the book didn't live up to my expectations.<br />Case Histories concerned 3 cold cases that Jackson Brodie has been hired to solve. Jackson Brodie used to be a police inspector but now works as a private investigator. The 3 cases all intersect at some point. One case is especially shocking.<br />I watched the TV series based on this book but it only lasted 2 years. Jackson Brodie was always getting in trouble in both the book and the TV series.<br />I will most likely read more by Kate Atkinson.</span>

<div id="review_179306156" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179306156" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1632609-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307368032p2/1632609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179306156?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/1632609-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179306156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16497262230345319620">I really liked this. It's not your conventional detective mystery; despite a missing toddler and two murders, its emphasis is on the characters rather than the crimes.<br/><br/>Detective Jackson Brodie is dealing with his own emotional baggage, as are the various family members of the three cold cases he's investigating. The result is tragic, quirky, confusing, surprising, frustrating, compelling. I read it in two sittings, such is its complex pull.<br/><br/>Recommended if you like something a little different.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3298771285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3298771285" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93114967-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551265103p2/93114967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3298771285?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/93114967-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781616813758" href="/book/show/9528971-case-histories">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3298771285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11691395346005547620">I'd never read Kate Atkinson when this book came up as a group read, so I was glad for the opportunity to see for myself whether this series was as good as I'd heard. I wasn't disappointed.<br/><br/>There was definitely a lot to like. The writing is first rate, the dialog well done, and the exposition of multiple concurrent plots is well executed. For the most part the characters - particularly the women, I think - were well conceived.<br/><br/>However, it did seem a bit cluttered, given all the characters of the t</span>
  <span id="freeText11691395346005547620" style="display:none">I'd never read Kate Atkinson when this book came up as a group read, so I was glad for the opportunity to see for myself whether this series was as good as I'd heard. I wasn't disappointed.<br /><br />There was definitely a lot to like. The writing is first rate, the dialog well done, and the exposition of multiple concurrent plots is well executed. For the most part the characters - particularly the women, I think - were well conceived.<br /><br />However, it did seem a bit cluttered, given all the characters of the three main cases PI Jackson Brodie is investigating, plus two less complex cases and his personal life. I found myself having to pause occasionally to sort out who belonged to which plot. And a plot line that resulted in repeated threats to Brodie's life seemed a bit off-key to me. From an overall perspective I can see how it was useful in bringing the entire book to a close, but it wasn't consistent with the more realistic nature of the other crimes.<br /><br />The ending of the book, actually, was something of a disappointment. A little too much good fortune coming out of nowhere for my tastes, but not enough to detract from a solid 4 for the book overall.<br /><br />The narrator of the audiobook, Susan Jameson, strikes just the right tone. A perfect match.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11691395346005547620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mqjwKQG9p5qWNCXxR39f5KOEAzZa3CDnSmduyvnbyaygjpn7uuNu8jEfkZCwilU7ddvk/pRRroARGSh7NJg7Ng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GLPYfRH39Xmr2Btekd+VHUPJyVojEcWDm6i9tPV7nOcilbGvqqk8EQzzrz9mKp/ClZYuku2cS+TA1vsFODhufQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4111636038616585664">Kate Atkinson was born in York and now lives in Edinburgh. Her first novel, <i>Behind the Scenes at the Museum</i>, won the Whitbread Book of the Year Award and she has been a critically acclaimed international bestselling author ever since.<br/><br/>She is the author of a collection of short stories, <i>Not the End of the World</i>, and of the critically acclaimed novels <i>Human Croquet</i>, <i>Emotionally Weird</i>, <i>Case Histories</i>,</span>
  <span id="freeText4111636038616585664" style="display:none">Kate Atkinson was born in York and now lives in Edinburgh. Her first novel, <i>Behind the Scenes at the Museum</i>, won the Whitbread Book of the Year Award and she has been a critically acclaimed international bestselling author ever since.<br /><br />She is the author of a collection of short stories, <i>Not the End of the World</i>, and of the critically acclaimed novels <i>Human Croquet</i>, <i>Emotionally Weird</i>, <i>Case Histories</i>, and <i>One Good Turn</i>.<br /><br /><i>Case Histories</i> introduced her readers to Jackson Brodie, former police inspector turned private investigator, and won the Saltire Book of the Year Award and the Prix Westminster. <br /><br />When Will There Be Good News? was voted Richard &amp; Judy Book Best Read of the Year. After Case Histories and One Good Turn, it was her third novel to feature the former private detective Jackson Brodie, who makes a welcome return in Started Early, Took My Dog. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4111636038616585664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
